et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and hold it between, and do not pierce just to the finger that is at the foundation, and place a thick covering of flesh or skin between your finger and the holding, and you will see the fistula at the one who teaches the covering from the hollow of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and cut beforehand near the holding, and then apply the cautery, until it reaches the head of the holding;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and it will be delivered the tent, and it will fall; then I will show you those withered fingers that seem a bird's pen, and none of them will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound does not heal, and it is short between you and the joint, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cauterizes gather these bone things: it is to know, the dryness of these joined fingers, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat the swollen tents in mud or in broken chozes, as long as the joints gather wound, and issue forth the dry fingers in the wound.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then heal the wound of the fingers suddenly inflamed by burning charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes near the fontanelle of the fundament, and is separated from the body, then apply your finger or fundament, and inquire into that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between two is the cloth or the syphac or flesh, or it is near to piercing, if there are no other ways than the way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	where you apply the cautery as we have said, or you cut just to the deep, or if you can then put tente and cure as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in the wound, so you do not cut the tendons that hold the foundation, and come to the passages by way of the intended sensation;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the cure, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healthy, or you remove that covering and the bandage then that it is cut from the deep foundation, or by tente or another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then define this faulty chart which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study how to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the weak part of the foundation: if it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And often fistulas are according to this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is where the foundation of the wound beneath the skin is touched.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a perforated tent according to this form at the head:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And thrust the twisted thread into the fistula, and thrust the tent into the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin of the fundament within, then extract the thread from that pierced one, so that you thrust your finger or fundament;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw the head of the thread, and assemble the fistula heads together, and hold one to the other, and let it stay there for a day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no more than once, until the threads grasp those flesh that are between the two, and hold fast;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound so that it becomes sound and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make a copper plate for the ulcer's dressing too deep inside, and then heal it, as we have said, so that it becomes healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinal abscess which makes the fistula is very sharp and pointed, piercing and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, because one does not see what one should not see, if you see it thus.
des emorroydes	of the wounds
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Wounds are of two kinds: either they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they immediately shed blood.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more of them, and they are deep in the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are deep have little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and immediately afterwards either a little citrine water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them deep in the foundation, it is that you instruct the patient to spread out on a chamber bed, until the foundations issue forth, and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and you hold it like a nail, or you hold it at your finger, then you cut into its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and the uncleanness cannot hold them by their moisture, if you take them with a drapil, or a cotton, or a piece of chamelot cloth;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and hold them in both hands, then cover, and sprinkle above some warm powders that are on the level of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then heal with other treatments until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot issue forth, then cleanse the patient of cleansing clusters biting and harsh to wash what is in the foundation, so that they can open up clearly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient takes hold, and if their veins are far from the foundation, then it is a light treatment;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you prick them with your thumb or the nails, and cut, then cure as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear not the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you make the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pass through from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too loose; and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one for correcting the excessive blood flow.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a piece of cloth, either a milliet cloth or one soaked in oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest until it heals, and when they are healed, if the treatment of ointment and other treatments, until it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	you must drain thoroughly at the bottom or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is draining of flux in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you make a poultice at the point of a spatula or on an angle to dry out the eczema above, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then the treatment as long as it is swollen so it needs.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be treated, then recommence the rubbing more strongly than before, as long as it hurts a lot and becomes scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment as long as it is healthy.
dou fremit	due to trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A blister is a small faulty appearance on the body, and goes much in depth.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the frost, and one feels it as if dead from cold, and it comes in all the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a thread of an owl's feather, or a strong bird's feather, and place that thread on the frost, so that the purple circles encircle the frost entirely around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all along the thread so that you grasp all around the frost, and insert it deeply, and remove the frost from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a cane of iron or copper according to this form, and be subtle underneath and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, for you must hold at the finger, and press; And if you see, cauterize the frenum, as it is before or in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a cluster of silver or copper, or of molten iron or mail; and never make these small and large instruments, according to those which are mentioned there.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These are the things one uses to treat children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema device is small and large above, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a separation or the belly is tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived inside; and it has on one side two holes, and on the other, one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly be where one puts the medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and let it be entirely surrounded by small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and has between each perforation, it should be widened, then push into these perforations a strong thread of twisted thread strongly turned in X or inquiring within, and assemble the belly as if it were a sack;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then attach the thread to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then cluster; and that's the circular form:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the cluster with oil or albumen of egg, or similar thing, then push it in gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then sprinkle the ministers with his two hands together, as much as it is all visible, then extract the cluster, and lift the patient's legs to the partition;
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he takes the medicine willingly, so much as he can; and if he sleeps one night completely, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse him of the disease of bowel disorder, and the medicine hastens to be issued, so recommend it as much as he may be healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the foundation, or abscess, so let the enema be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about manual and medical treatments, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations or where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing of stone, and cutting with a sword or a knife, or with a lance or a stick or an arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where they are made according to the laws of the body, as if a wound falls on the neck, or on the head, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care it's not a matter of stones or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you suspect a slight abscess: if you make it healthier from the cephalic membrane immediately, as if blood comes out of the wound, and let the healing be contrary to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from repletion of wine and of coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to recover, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine, nor eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, apply a poultice of cotton soaked in rose oil soothingly, or with wine stippled.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, so that it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will discuss a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and he arms are numb, if you put on some bandages, so they become healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be assembled by tugging, then assemble them by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, from the suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it is deep, and only holds for a little while, then cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore the hard skin in place of the skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, like boiled and roasted meat, and also as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a putrid wound, and it has not attached to the bone, so cut out all the putridness, and throw it away, then heal;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has entered into the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, so seek to cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not benefit at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which soothes in this way that the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; lively chalk three parts, and powder subtly,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the plaster, and hold it firmly, until it adheres well and joins with all its sap;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it tightly, and leave it without loosening, so it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never does one make a poultice of chalk solely, when one has not incense nor dragon's blood, but rather the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has become putrid, meanwhile in this state, if you do not put this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of flour of barley mixed with water and honey, until it discharges pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal other wounds as long as they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then remove it with subtle pinces.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be soothing, if you heat it in warm water, and mix it with rose oil, and cook it in warm water as well;
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other mines of a similar kind, prepared in this manner, and applied with moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, prick below or further down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and a flow of blood comes, then open it, and purge it, and cauterize, for this is his profession;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conduit is guarded, because that's where the flesh goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the jugular vein on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it steadily, and let it have some days, then heal the wounds completely so that it becomes healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, remove the broken ones you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound putrefies;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful and adjust the outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then treat it as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if the wound is ventilating, how much the patient is suffering: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it tightly by the blood that does not congeal yet.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the body, and open the patient's eye;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and bind it several times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, then put much cotton into the wound to suck up the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and have the patient sleep on the wound for two or three days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there will not come a spasm, nor evil trembling of heart nor bad signs from the vein.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds with tents and other treatments, until they are healthy.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if she cannot heal, and make effort, at least know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has caught pieces, then examine the wound, and remove the false fibers if they are severed.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not severed, then let the wound purify, and alleviate the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	because of the obstruction of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The obstructions of the belly are great and mean and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound often the intestine, or the knots of the intestines, because of the intrusion of it;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more painful, and often worse than the small wound than the great one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Because one must put back together the intestines in, so that they are not repeatedly reset from hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell so much that they feel cold, if they return again to the points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it wants to soften the moist wound, because one must reset the intestine to its place that is suitable for others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The common stitches have an effect on the stitch of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitches for other wounds of the body and these specific stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and however they are more suitable with the stitch of the belly, and I will describe one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine is outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and this thing is to put back, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	for the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wrap a sponge or a lot of cloth in water to soothe it thoroughly,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you apply a hot poultice and cupping glasses and a spike,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and lift the intestine until the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at no time should these veins be constricted, and it is necessary that they be freed from inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the inflammation depart, if you calm the intestine of water or wine and bad humors are cleansed,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for it is aligned with the entrance to a small extent;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound at the instrument by which one gathers the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to remove what is superfluous,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we must not cut without great necessity there is;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and it's the instruments for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within the curvature and do not deviate, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	If you reset it according to its natural form in its own place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	See you then have power, for that is worth much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the part beneath the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	then you must make the patient sit up on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is on the lower part beneath the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if you place the head and the foot higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and thus the rupture of the belly is in one of the injured parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	you intend to understand in this that the numb part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus you should minister to it, as I say, in great and tender wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	In small wounds you put that which is prepared for you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then hold it in your hands, I minister piteously who pulls out all the routing from his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and gather the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it is the common manner of stitches,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you prick with a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound, that is to say, a thread of space, and fix a needle or it has a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the syringe,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, until you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two heads of the syringe with the three assembled;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then stretch a double thread inside the needle of two parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the edges of the wound together immediately
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let the space of the fingers, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then thread it with a double strand as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this according to how you have mastered the use of needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the whole wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the subtle needles take in all the flesh, and those that are too large cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because it is suitable that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and do not want to push the needles too deep into the flesh and two layers of skin
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so they don't touch and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then touch the heads of the needles, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I hold taut or drape on the heads of the needles to keep them steady,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it suffices to sew with one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you bring together the two heads of leather and the two heads of silk, assembling them into a needle where there is a strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced these two heads assembled together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then push the needle to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews the drapes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	This treatment follows the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I treated a wound that one of my men had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a dagger,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width deep,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and let the intestines well .ij. palms of great,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and it was the wound in the midst of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine then when it had been .xxiiij. hours outside,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up just to .xv. days, and it was cured, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not care for his ointment, because I was in a place where they found none, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and applied it above the wound with a cotton cloth many times a day, and washed it with warm honey water until he was healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and prick the part that is defective just up to that spot within.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart in a straight line, if there the head of the needle or you have pricked with the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make a piercing from another part of the defective area just up to that spot within.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew thus as the tailor makes the pelts,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you let one side of the siphac rest, and take it up again on another side, until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of stitching, which Galen properly describes,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	it is like a fountain that naturally assembles the broken parts together,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and applies one head of the siphac to another head, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or a pointed instrument, and make it penetrate slightly.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the heads of the juices flow;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it penetrate from the weak part just up to the dense area within.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the heads of the juices flow;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make a perforation on one side and the other of the weak part just up to the inner skin, in other heads of wonder that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen said this in his book, and no one contradicts him,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew up the belly with two needles, or have a thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must thrust a needle from one side, and another from the other, in the manner of those who sew up wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and it is known that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if the stitching is more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, thus the arrow has moved.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you put back in order the intestine, and sew up the cut; then apply the powder irritating flesh,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and the arrow has moved, if you put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and pull out the thread, and sew up the seam, and the membrane;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal the wound as the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, put them on, at once, so that they begin to heal the swelling, very much.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and remove it several times a day, until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicines in addition to these dispositions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if it is necessary that you apply a light bandage in oil of temperament warm, or in oil of rose,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the angles, and below the spines;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or prickling in the belly, and many times it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If they cauterize with black wine, and meanwhile the purification reaches just up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is due to the abundance of veins that are there, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the swelling falls from the wound, reset it back as it was originally, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned black or dark, it is necessary to lay the black spot that removes blood that comes from it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the indices of the head while parting the skin beneath the wound until it reaches to align the extraction when the nerves are severed, and the wound is swollen.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture from the swelling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced in the belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and in this way the excretion and flatulence ceased;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I knew, and did not cease from subtling until he was healthy, and the limb was sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sweat, I doubted that the patient had bad things in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no point of evil, but he remained in better conditions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied up in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm holds on great tests, then assemble the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the patient has opened his mouth, if he puts it on the two lips
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if he stretches his mouth upwards;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he cuts the top of the head, and this is held so that it cannot be dislocated,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another ferrum in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	Although it settles in the intestine, and brings no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	Take the head of this intestine thread that is very much disentangled,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then attach it to the head of this thread, i.e. the subtle twisted thread of flax,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and reset it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing the fractures is not beyond what is according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, so there is no engineer who can heal it, because of subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whether it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes swollen, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it is split and has an open sore.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the true nodulation of a hard and white ulcer, where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also shaved like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear and smooth skin, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not clean, and there is no flesh.
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not except by one of the seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, by the small passage of blood or flow;
ou por sa malice;	or by its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	Here is the translation:
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the flesh is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where because the corruption is a type of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	for the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow healing, and weak by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already demonstrated all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I teach you about the treatment of fistula which is done by surgical operation with hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	where it is in the skin, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in one of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if a part comes to the ownership of the principal member, and its similar limbs.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the ulcers that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no ulcer that does not approach just to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you will recognize the signs, if you take a tent of iron or steel, the ulcer is straight, if it is sought;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, seek a subtle thread of probe.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the probes bend themselves inward towards the twisting.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many passages and you cannot examine it well by probing,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse it through one of the passages,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture flows from one part to another, and it infects;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then the wound heals at your power, that you know if there is a bone or nerve, and it is shaved away in the background,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	where among those places that I told you, if the head according to what I told you
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and bone for the fracture and the corrupted cartilages that are within
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healthy
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well perforated in the right place, then you must cut in a perpendicular direction, as much as you can
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I have often used medicines in the treatment of fever, and applied them just at the head of the abscess.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the excess which is accumulated at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I have put ointments on the wounded flesh, so that it may be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healthy through this, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if his bone is corrupted by the fistula, thus he copes.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not grieve or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, thus you should remove it until the decay is entirely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the affected areas as much as possible so that they are healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not sane, and render void thus as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet healed just at the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and search as long as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus healthy, it's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this does not work, know that the corruption is too deep-seated, so you cannot come to an end;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with bandages,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if he withdraws from an instrument suitable for this,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if he has many bones, if they are drawn apart, do not leave one behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you cut and moisten and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot dislodge them within an hour, then place on the wound a poultice that induces putrefaction.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the abscess is rotten between the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have more lightly touched bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the thigh or leg,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove so much of the corruption until the blackness is entirely eliminated,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corrupted body, and it reaches just below the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if you want to sew and cover everything just up to the corruption, and then cure it as long as it is swollen;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that had occurred to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about thirty years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matters came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and he had no way to cure it by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the mirror shows by their foolish work so much that the abscesses open,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corrupt many materials, and become fistulas, and they come from many perforations that all go bad and moist in the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many mirrors mirrored a cure for 12 years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they cured him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and this which corrodes through the pores to a large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man becomes red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I touched a tent in one of these pores, and then I searched all the pores,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one vein came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings as far as I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came right up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I suspected that it was separated from the corrupted bone, and I thought that there would be no other corruption, except for that which I had seen;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicines applied slowly over a long period of time, and could not heal it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I examined him, and discovered the bone as it was beforehand,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and the putridity, and then I stopped it, and thought to reunite the limb;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do more than I cupped under a palm of the bone, and I pulled it out with all its thickness,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he was quickly healed and recovered hastily,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it is no longer possible to continue the work because of the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for fear of death that I have of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the evacuation of blood is often unsuccessful, but it was completely healthy,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard crust formed on the wound, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction in any way, neither to heal nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take the bandage, and hold it at the head of the bone which opens,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct him to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another bandage of a larger size than the first one, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and hold the head steady, if you treat the corrupt flesh at the bottom,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the joint where you see the swelling, so that the swelling does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a splint or a table underneath the bone to support the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to swell thus so that one can see and feel the corruption, and swell again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if it discovers the whole flesh; then put the fire cautery underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sew one part to the other against the corruption, and let the sewing be from the length of the corruption, a little, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and sew the bone or where it connects to the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other anguish than to cover twice;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is a prick in the hand, or a prick in the foot, it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however it behooves you to investigate this corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and the Mondified in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not do harm to you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and it is known that the surgeons and the wise men for coping with these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the wounds.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each similarity of work with his instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and it is known that the workshop will show you the instrument which you will have need of, according to the knowledge of this art;
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument with which you operate according to what it needs.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head protrudes either because of inward pressure or because of outward force;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that corrosion through the treatment of medicines, it does not benefit.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cover that member up to the place or where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes death through this, or through evil, which is a greater fault of the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then proceed after the bruise, then go those corroding members from member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and take hold of the entire body; if you hasten to couple,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, like a sea scorpion and viper and similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the finger, then couple it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, if the cope is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach just to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, if the cope is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it does not deserve any remedies other than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and all thus done when the corrosion comes or falls: if it comes to the first joint, then the cope after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, so cover the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up to the leg, so cover to the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, so there is no other remedy than to let the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to cover or to soothe the limb is that you tie it above and below;
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch out one minister's hand downwards, and another minister's hand upwards.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you separate the flesh that is between the two ligaments at a spacious interval, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then apply the dressing or bandage, and put a layer of linen cloth on each part, so that the dressing does not touch the healthy skin;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another lesion and abscess from the wound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if the flow of blood comes when you operate, then cauterize the place quickly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then wrap the numb member with a suitable lien, and treat it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will count how many steps he has in his own foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed to be burnt by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in his finger by the foot, so much that it took over the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was saved;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corrosion returned to the finger of the hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on things rebounding after the purification of the body, and cannot stop the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it is seen that I grasp his hand, and I do not want, that I had hoped to rebound the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and also doubted whether I cut off his hand, so that he would not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he grasps his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not found it recounted that because of this they make another part, so one has mastery over it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does an abscess come to the raw flesh, and stays for a long time, causing a great accumulation of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, and the veins become empty, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is also as subtle as the delicate sheets
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not rub against the bone, nor against the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy"
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula"
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so enlarged that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the curator is such that you grasp the whole circle, and similarly when it is subtle, just like a drapier.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not be mistaken because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the curators are hardened, and the corruption is not on the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the curator is specially chosen for flesh, if the cure of the fistula is thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Here is the translation:
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then theclysterizer of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take galena, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put copper into the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it into water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and to cleanse the wound, and hold back the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay there for two hours, then strain it by pressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the wound is made clean, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time is cleansing done with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of wood from vine, and throw water upon them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then boil, and clarify, until you know that the serum is well purified;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if you clarify with water and honey, or it has a little bit of litharge broth;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	where you apply a mixture of honey and wine, which has the property of softening and cleansing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the wounds are well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if you apply a mixture of what makes flesh grow in them,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have mentioned the properties or treatments of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the hole in the sinus is small, and the cane of the cleansing cannot enter;
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you enlarge it with an iron a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment;
